  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_3e27681b-13af-4717-b616-c41464b751c6'
      });
    }

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer106117611" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5655726003003640793">I originally read Ashes In The Wind back in 1979.<br/>I remember the date because I had just come home from the hospital with my first born Michael, who finally tied the knot this month with his partner and has given me two beautiful granddaughters.<br/>Since this was another special moment in time, I decided to pick this "keeper" I had given five stars to back up to see if time had changed with how I felt then..and now.<br/>Truthfully, I cant remember any of it...is it a wonder between feeding's, diaper chang</span>
  <span id="freeText5655726003003640793" style="display:none">I originally read Ashes In The Wind back in 1979.<br />I remember the date because I had just come home from the hospital with my first born Michael, who finally tied the knot this month with his partner and has given me two beautiful granddaughters.<br />Since this was another special moment in time, I decided to pick this "keeper" I had given five stars to back up to see if time had changed with how I felt then..and now.<br />Truthfully, I cant remember any of it...is it a wonder between feeding's, diaper changes, no sleep,and one colic infant? <br />I do remember snatching every moment I could to get in a chapter or two, and I think escaping into Alaina and Cole's world kept me sane. <br />Did the passage of time and my tastes that have changed over the years lessen the magic of their romantic story? <br />Was I swept away and able to escape once again? <br />Did it live up to the five stars I had given it back then?<br />Darn tooting it did!<br />Some books remain timeless, back onto my "favourite keeper" shelf...till we read again :):)</span>
  <a data-text-id="5655726003003640793" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <span id="freeText4836124371549819411" style="display:none"><b><br />This one is tough for me to rate because there are some parts of this book I LOVED, and some I absolutely HATED!!<br /><br />First I have to say that I really enjoy the author's writing style, it's so much different from the modern books that it's like in another universe.         <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/112347251?book_show_action=true">Jul 19, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Vivian" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Vivian" href="/user/show/3947172-vivian">Vivian</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3947172-vivian?shelf=dragon-s-hoard">dragon-s-hoard</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3947172-vivian?shelf=romance-hist">romance-hist</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer112347251" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3127079591168776989">This was a reread after many, many years--and it held up to my memory. <br/><br/>I originally read this as a young teen and loved it. Rereading it as an adult I was wondering if it was going to be as good as I remembered, and while it wandered far afield, but at over 600 pages you have room for a story to stretch time and space, it was entertaining. I definitely understand why I liked it as a young woman. Alaina was so much of what I identified with at that age and aspired to from the metamorphosis from t</span>
  <span id="freeText3127079591168776989" style="display:none">This was a reread after many, many years--and it held up to my memory. <br /><br />I originally read this as a young teen and loved it. Rereading it as an adult I was wondering if it was going to be as good as I remembered, and while it wandered far afield, but at over 600 pages you have room for a story to stretch time and space, it was entertaining. I definitely understand why I liked it as a young woman. Alaina was so much of what I identified with at that age and aspired to from the metamorphosis from tomboy into beautiful young woman, the heroine--she's pulling the hero out of scrapes multiple times, not sitting back wilting and waiting, some fantastic friends, and some less than stellar family. I admired her fortitude and definitely had her smart mouth. <br /><br />The Civil War is not a romantic period and this book spends more time dealing with the realities of shortages and renderings of medical care and issues (varnished), albeit far behind lines, but you get bone saw and various triage arguments. You get the wretched feelings of being torn apart by loyalties and ideas of decency and when they get sacrificed. You get the consequences of death and permanent injury and pain. All this in a bodice ripper? Yep. <br /><br /><b>
  <i>"I have always been suspicious of this flaring thing that occurs on first glance," he muttered. He favored her with a quick glance and spoke with deliberate slowness. "How can I determine what love is? When a man and a woman begin to understand each other, love begins small and grows with the passage of time. It is that which a man holds within himself until it blooms to its fullest."</i>
</b><br /><br />Being a romance, you get to eat your cake and have it too. So while all these things are happening to the characters you don't leave them in a casket, which was nice. I read grim, we see grim every day on the news so having something that takes you through hell and back again with a happy ending is kinda nice, right now. <br /><br /><b>
  <i>Two beings wrapped in the pure bliss of their union, proceeding in eager, uncaring haste, giving all to the other and in return finding everything and more.<i></i></i>
</b><br /><br />My rating remains four stars.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3127079591168776989" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3395786068" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3395786068" />
    <a title="✩ Yaz ✩" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/76194326-yaz"><img alt="✩ Yaz ✩" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1593729638p2/76194326.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3395786068?book_show_action=true">Aug 19, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="✩ Yaz ✩" class="user" itemprop="url" name="✩ Yaz ✩" href="/user/show/76194326-yaz">✩ Yaz ✩</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/76194326-yaz?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/76194326-yaz?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/76194326-yaz?shelf=adult">adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3395786068" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18070319599892173900">4 - ⭐️⭐️⭐️⭐️<br/><br/><b>Ashes in the Wind</b> was a pleasant surprise! It got my heart fluttering and pounding with its extremely slow-burn romance and in agitation of unforeseen circumstances<br/><br/>I was spellbound by <b>Kathleen E. Woodiwiss’s fluid writing</b>. I was wholly immersed in what I consider to be a heavy romance book without it being a daunting experience because the writing alone just flows beautifully.<br/><br/>The <b>romance</b> was a chaotic whirlwind! The blazing chemistry between <b>Alaina</b> and <b>Cole</b>, because I would not descr</span>
  <span id="freeText18070319599892173900" style="display:none">4 - ⭐️⭐️⭐️⭐️<br /><br /><b>Ashes in the Wind</b> was a pleasant surprise! It got my heart fluttering and pounding with its extremely slow-burn romance and in agitation of unforeseen circumstances<br /><br />I was spellbound by <b>Kathleen E. Woodiwiss’s fluid writing</b>. I was wholly immersed in what I consider to be a heavy romance book without it being a daunting experience because the writing alone just flows beautifully.<br /><br />The <b>romance</b> was a chaotic whirlwind! The blazing chemistry between <b>Alaina</b> and <b>Cole</b>, because I would not describe in any other way, engulfed me. The slow-burn was truly excruciating because trust me when I say it. was. SLOW. Yet, it was rewarding once they sheathed their claws and their hearts began to soften for one another. Though I have to say I enjoyed their banter and teasing, but half of the time I found it to be vexing because it burst my lovey-dovey bubbles whenever there was a perfect romantic moment, they managed to ruin it somehow. As for the characters themselves, I really liked Alaina but she played with my nerves a lot. As for Cole, I had mixed feelings about him, I liked him in the first quarter of the book, began to have very mixed feelings about him by the end of Part 1 but I grew to like him more in Part 2.<br /><br />As for the <b>plot</b>, I would say it was a bumpy ride. Unlike other romances, this one has a more serious tone to it and the circumstances do not get easier for the characters although I felt like there were events that were a little too convenient for the characters. It was probably 30% to 50% through the story that I felt it’s becoming a little flat and the pacing did not help but it managed to keep me interested for the other half of the book which I believe has the best bits.<br /><br />Despite the few points I wasn’t happy about, I would recommend this book but keep in mind that it’s roughly around 600 pages and it’s a heavy read in terms of the story. I promise you if you love slow-burn romances, this will satisfy your craving for a true slow-burn.</span>
  <a data-text-id="18070319599892173900" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_104981635" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

    <a title="Carolyn F." class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2624012-carolyn-f"><img alt="Carolyn F." src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1521926478p2/2624012.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/104981635?book_show_action=true">May 31, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Carolyn F." class="user" itemprop="url" name="Carolyn F." href="/user/show/2624012-carolyn-f">Carolyn F.</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2624012-carolyn-f?shelf=not-kept">not-kept</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2624012-carolyn-f?shelf=historical-romance">historical-romance</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer104981635" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2949589075248200400">What a book! As I was reading it, parts started coming back to me and I used to read a lot of Woodiwiss in the early '80s so I must have read this book. The beginning was strange. The middle was horrible, I hated Alaina so much while reading this part. Could she never say anything nice to Cole?!? The last part of the novel was better and the ending was great. <br/><br/>Things that drove me crazy besides the above: Cole being rescued from the river - 2 times. Alaina literally running into Jacques - 4 times</span>
  <span id="freeText2949589075248200400" style="display:none">What a book! As I was reading it, parts started coming back to me and I used to read a lot of Woodiwiss in the early '80s so I must have read this book. The beginning was strange. The middle was horrible, I hated Alaina so much while reading this part. Could she never say anything nice to Cole?!? The last part of the novel was better and the ending was great. <br /><br />Things that drove me crazy besides the above: Cole being rescued from the river - 2 times. Alaina literally running into Jacques - 4 times! Give me a break. Could the author not come up with anything different. And the male blacks were portrayed as - well just awful! This is the 1980s not the 1880s, or even the 1930s. I kind of understand writing how you think they may have sounded, but I'm sure they could speak in sentences and were not unintelligent. I don't think the author realizes that <b>all</b> human beings have brains and are able to use them - some better than most but still. Okay, so you can see that was a HUGE peeve for me. <br /><br />I don't think I'll read this book again. I'm only giving this book 2.5 stars. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="2949589075248200400" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer283245185" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer12878694713623389537">Captivating Civil War Romance!<br/><br/>When Kathleen Woodiwiss did romance well, there was no one better--and such a novel is ASHES IN THE WIND. To my thinking, it's up there with her best (THE FLAME AND THE FLOWER, THE WOLF AND THE DOVE and SHANNA).<br/><br/>It is a compelling tale of a young Southern woman from Louisiana who loses everything in the Civil War. The Yankees take her family and her home and finally, even her identity. Disguised as a boy for her safety, 17-year old Alaina MacGaren thinks to seek refu</span>
  <span id="freeText12878694713623389537" style="display:none">Captivating Civil War Romance!<br /><br />When Kathleen Woodiwiss did romance well, there was no one better--and such a novel is ASHES IN THE WIND. To my thinking, it's up there with her best (THE FLAME AND THE FLOWER, THE WOLF AND THE DOVE and SHANNA).<br /><br />It is a compelling tale of a young Southern woman from Louisiana who loses everything in the Civil War. The Yankees take her family and her home and finally, even her identity. Disguised as a boy for her safety, 17-year old Alaina MacGaren thinks to seek refuge in her uncle's home in New Orleans. But before she can reach him she encounters a group of soldiers who harass her. She is saved from them by a young Yankee surgeon, Captain Cole Latimer from Minnesota, a man of honor and great medical talent who is respectful of Southerners. <br /><br />Cole takes "Al" the boy (Alaina's new identity) under his wing and gives "him" a job at the Yankee army hospital in New Orleans Al returns the favor and saves the doctor's life one night when he is drunk, set upon by thieves and tossed into the Mississippi River. In the process of caring for Cole in her uncle's home, much happens, and a great mix-up occurs that casts a shadow on the rest of the story.<br /><br />It is a magnificent love story, well told with great plot twists and accurate history of the era, woven in so that you understand what is going on in the Civil War. Her characters are richly drawn. You will feel you are living it and you will celebrate Alaina's strength and intelligence. She plays many parts and Woodiwiss does them all so well. You won't regret reading this one--it's a keeper!<br /><br />Here's the backlist should you want to read more. It seems from my own experience and others that the earlier books (look at the dates) are the best.<br /><br />Birmingham Family Saga Series<br /><br />The Flame and the Flower, 1972 (her first and one of her best)<br /> Short story, "The Kiss<br /> Short story, "Beyond the Kiss" <br />A Season Beyond a Kiss, 2000<br />The Elusive Flame, 1998<br /><br />Single Novels<br /><br />The Wolf and the Dove, 1974<br />Shanna, 1977<br />Ashes in the Wind, 1979<br />A Rose in Winter, 1981<br />Come Love a Stranger, 1984<br />So Worthy My Love, 1989<br />Forever in Your Embrace, 1992<br />Petals on the River, 1997<br />The Reluctant Suitor, 2002<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="12878694713623389537" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer1781156853997438956">This was one of the first romance books I read when I was twelve. I didn't have any triggers or any real opinions about romance and romance books back then. Somehow I made my way through this book. Thinking back, I don't know why I wasn't as shocked and angry about how some the events played out. It was a very enjoyable book I remember, but dang...some of the plot points in this really pisses me off. The main one concerning the hero and the heroine's cousin. Ugh. Why?! Not my favorite by her. </span>

  <span id="freeText8383586990082832671" style="display:none"><b>*Re-read*<br />*Buddy read with Blacky &lt;3&lt;3&lt;3*</b><br /><br />Over the last twenty years I read this book many times, this was my first time in English and it still is one of my all time favorites. <br /><br />I just <b>LOVE</b> Al/Alaina &amp; Cole. <div id="review_90308274" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/90308274" />
    <a title="Patrick" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1458187-patrick"><img alt="Patrick" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1219632090p2/1458187.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/90308274?book_show_action=true">Feb 18, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Patrick" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Patrick" href="/user/show/1458187-patrick">Patrick</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780786209484" href="/book/show/5047875-ashes-in-the-wind">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer90308274" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6208056065504635434">The first romance novel I ever read, and still the best. I all but gulped and breathed it in voraciously, reading while eating, getting up during the night to see what would happen next, only to end up reading all night long, and sighed with satisfaction and gratification, in the afterglow of the end. I read it all, in 3 days. </span>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer16709341745676903581">"Ashes in the Wind" is set during the Civil War in the South and is about Alaina, a young Southern woman and a doctor who is a Union soldier. Alaina's life and home have been torn apart by the war and she is forced into disguising herself as a young boy "Al" to ward off unwanted attention and to work as a spy. This is a captivating saga that pulls you into the story and you will not want to put it down. You feel the aura of the Civil War around you as you read this book. Expect to experience a f</span>
  <span id="freeText16709341745676903581" style="display:none">"Ashes in the Wind" is set during the Civil War in the South and is about Alaina, a young Southern woman and a doctor who is a Union soldier. Alaina's life and home have been torn apart by the war and she is forced into disguising herself as a young boy "Al" to ward off unwanted attention and to work as a spy. This is a captivating saga that pulls you into the story and you will not want to put it down. You feel the aura of the Civil War around you as you read this book. Expect to experience a full gamut of emotions when you read this, and to close it with a smile and contentment.<br /><br />I have been a Kathleen Woodiwiss fan since the first book of hers that I picked up over 30 years ago and I believe I have read every book she has written. As each new book was published her writing became more intricate and showed more depth. I have enjoyed them all, but without a doubt this one was my favorite. My heart broke when she passed away a couple of years ago because I knew there would never again be another new Woodiwiss to snuggle into a chair with and read for hours. If you are not a fan of historical romances you may want to pass, but you will be missing a very good story. <br /><br /><br /><br /> </span>

<div id="review_111914113" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/111914113" />
    <a title="Bella Foxygobble" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3976165-bella-foxygobble"><img alt="Bella Foxygobble" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1438695517p2/3976165.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/111914113?book_show_action=true">Jul 16, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Bella Foxygobble" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Bella Foxygobble" href="/user/show/3976165-bella-foxygobble">Bella Foxygobble</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780688125028" href="/book/show/994306.Ashes_in_the_Wind">review of another edition</a>


          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Bella by: </span>
      bodice ripper group
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3976165-bella-foxygobble?shelf=2010-me">2010-me</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3976165-bella-foxygobble?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3976165-bella-foxygobble?shelf=historical-romance">historical-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3976165-bella-foxygobble?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3976165-bella-foxygobble?shelf=louisiana">louisiana</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3976165-bella-foxygobble?shelf=minnesota">minnesota</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3976165-bella-foxygobble?shelf=girl-in-pants">girl-in-pants</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3976165-bella-foxygobble?shelf=pub1979">pub1979</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer111914113" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4867432397012012351">Okay I guess I am ready to write my review for this book. Reading it was definitely a labor of love for me. I feel as though now that I've read my first Woodiwiss novel I can officially label myself a fan of the bodice-ripper genre. <br/><br/>That said, never in all my years of reading have I encountered a heroine I wanted to slap more than Alaina "Al" MacGaren. Admittedly, one of my biggest pet peeves in a story is the whole "girl-in-pants" deal. I can't wrap my head around the idea of a woman passing of</span>
  <span id="freeText4867432397012012351" style="display:none">Okay I guess I am ready to write my review for this book. Reading it was definitely a labor of love for me. I feel as though now that I've read my first Woodiwiss novel I can officially label myself a fan of the bodice-ripper genre. <br /><br />That said, never in all my years of reading have I encountered a heroine I wanted to slap more than Alaina "Al" MacGaren. Admittedly, one of my biggest pet peeves in a story is the whole "girl-in-pants" deal. I can't wrap my head around the idea of a woman passing off as a man for any long period of time. I didn't buy it in the movie Just One of The Guys, and I didn't buy it in Ashes in the Wind. <br /><br />The book starts off with Alaina fleeing her home dressed as Al because she is being accused of being a rebel spy. She journeys to her Uncle's home and along the way has an encounter with Cole Lattimer, the heroe of the story. He believes her guise as Al and gives her a job at the hospital he works at in New Orleans. She is able to keep up this sham for a good portion of the book. Being that as I stated earlier girls-in-pants don't do it for me, it made for a VERY long first half of the book.<br /><br />In the 2nd half of the book Cole &amp; Alaina eventually come together, but in true bodice-ripper fashion she makes every stupid cliche mistake a heroine could make. She's stubborn, runs away a lot, puts herself in danger and finally realizes almost too late how much she loves our hero Cole. Really she treated him like a piece of garbage for 75% of the book. It was like a really bad 80's horror flick, only bodice-ripper style. I kept waiting for Freddy Crueger to jump out from around the corner. <br /><br />And the hero Cole... sigh. I had very little respect for this man. He was bullied into a marriage he didn't really want in the beginning, and was very much the tortured "big-baby" hero for most of the 2nd half of the book. I just can't believe he was so blind and stupid he didn't figure out that Al was a actually a girl. And I hated the way Alaina treated him. He doesn't really pony up for me until the end, where it seems too little too late. <br /><br />Part I and Part II of this book really felt disconnected to me. They felt as though they were almost two completely different stories. Although I was completely bored with Part I, Part II really picked up the pace and was a much more enjoyable read. It was however, so completely over the top that it left me breathless at the end... I felt like I had just run the mile in highschool (that seems to take forever) and then just like that its done and time for a cold shower in the locker room with no cool-down time before its time for my next class. <br /><br />In the end I don't think this book was a complete waste of time for me. It did leave me with some enjoyable moments. It will not however, be a book that I will be re-reading any time soon. <br /><br />Rating: 2.5 stars. I'll rate it 3 stars here for the fact that the last 200 or so pages were VERY entertaining and true to the art form of bodice-ripper writing. <br />Warning: Rape scene<br /><br />My Ratings:<br /><br />5*****I loved this book, consider it an all time favorite<br />4**** Thoroughly enjoyed the book and will recommend it<br />3*** I liked it well enough,<br />2** Brain Candy - It was okay. Writing mediocre, will<br />keep/re-read if part of a series<br />1* didn't like/possibly not finished. (less)</span>
  <a data-text-id="4867432397012012351" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_810748226" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/810748226" />
    <a title="Cheap and Lazy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/17565563-cheap-and-lazy"><img alt="Cheap and Lazy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1361148454p2/17565563.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/810748226?book_show_action=true">Jan 03, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cheap and Lazy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cheap and Lazy" href="/user/show/17565563-cheap-and-lazy">Cheap and Lazy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17565563-cheap-and-lazy?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17565563-cheap-and-lazy?shelf=historical-not-regency">historical-not-regency</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer810748226" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7280706694812415836">Kathleen Woodiwiss Classic. If you’re unable to set aside sensibilities for a romance of this age (first published in 1979), find bodice-rippers in general, or cross-dressing heroines particularly distasteful or implausible, your reading time will likely be spent more happily elsewhere. Typical of Kathleen Woodiwiss, this is a long—nearly epic—tale. <br/><br/>For the rest of us: <br/>I’m a fan of this author for several reasons, not the least of which is that she’s the mother of historical romance as we know i</span>
  <span id="freeText7280706694812415836" style="display:none">Kathleen Woodiwiss Classic. If you’re unable to set aside sensibilities for a romance of this age (first published in 1979), find bodice-rippers in general, or cross-dressing heroines particularly distasteful or implausible, your reading time will likely be spent more happily elsewhere. Typical of Kathleen Woodiwiss, this is a long—nearly epic—tale. <br /><br />For the rest of us: <br />I’m a fan of this author for several reasons, not the least of which is that she’s the mother of historical romance as we know it today. Without the bodice-ripper, we would not have the more socially acceptable versions being written now. Although she does wax a bit too descriptive and occasionally repetitive for my tastes, unnecessary scenes and characters do crop up from time to time, and her heroines are always intensely moral and hardworking (think Dickens), they are also intelligent and strong, and Ms. Woodiwiss’s overall story-telling is simply unparalleled. Additionally, I appreciate her use of varying perspectives within scenes to tell her stories more effectively. I’ve noticed this technique has become rare in more recently published books. <br /><br />The Civil War background is both emotionally and impartially drawn (no small feat, that). The various roles young southern lady Alaina plays come through believably, especially through the eyes of our honorable and somewhat hapless Yankee doctor hero, Cole. The beginning, and most, of the story takes place in Louisiana (especially New Orleans), and ends in Minnesota. That the author was born in the former and lived many years in the latter comes through in the authentic details of the settings and the liberal sprinkling of dialects/accents of the respective inhabitants. <br /><br />The story offers a core mystery well wrapped in several others, plenty of action, suspense, romantic moments (though not as many love scenes as readers like me might hope), and a wonderfully satisfying ending. I love that Alaina saves Cole’s life, twice (!), instead of the other way around. I think some of the misunderstandings and angst were drawn out, while others felt rushed over, but that’s a matter of my taste and perspective. All in all, I really enjoyed the book and recommend it to fans of Woodiwiss who haven’t gotten around to it yet (I can’t be the only one, right?) and any reader who wants to explore a classic of this era in romance. </span>
  <a data-text-id="7280706694812415836" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/247400428" />
    <a title="Rich Meyer" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4585903-rich-meyer"><img alt="Rich Meyer" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442485356p2/4585903.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/247400428?book_show_action=true">Dec 15, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rich Meyer" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rich Meyer" href="/user/show/4585903-rich-meyer">Rich Meyer</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4585903-rich-meyer?shelf=read-in-2011">read-in-2011</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer247400428" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7900342914654418777">Boy, I really have to start thinking before I read books on a dare...<br/><br/>Oddly enough, Ashes in the Wind wasn't nearly as horrid as I thought it would be. Predictable, yes. Characters of the stoutest cardboard, true. But I didn't mind the writing style as much as I thought I would. There was a bit too much description at times. Anyone who's seen Gone With the Wind, and who would be reading this book if they hadn't, should've been able to easily imagine each scene with a little less than what we are </span>
  <span id="freeText7900342914654418777" style="display:none">Boy, I really have to start thinking before I read books on a dare...<br /><br />Oddly enough, Ashes in the Wind wasn't nearly as horrid as I thought it would be. Predictable, yes. Characters of the stoutest cardboard, true. But I didn't mind the writing style as much as I thought I would. There was a bit too much description at times. Anyone who's seen Gone With the Wind, and who would be reading this book if they hadn't, should've been able to easily imagine each scene with a little less than what we are given. But luckily my years in Dickensian retreat prepared me quite well for that obstacle. <br /><br />Next time, I'm doing the daring, and someone's gonna end up reading William S. Burroughs or Hunter S. Thompson! You hear me, Cortesi! Naked Lunch! Fear and Loathing!</span>
  <a data-text-id="7900342914654418777" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2036118441?book_show_action=true">Jun 21, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Wyldrabbit" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Wyldrabbit" href="/user/show/4047771-wyldrabbit">Wyldrabbit</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2036118441" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6058076722813632250">I still cannot believe I am giving a Woodiwiss book only 2 stars. It seemed to me that part one and part two were written at completely different times. Alaina jumps back and forth between really caring for Cole, to not at all. There seemed to be so many plot lines throughout the book, that the characters suffered for it. The unlikely events that happened to coincide with one another were unbelievable at best, and the villains in the story were not thought out. I never felt connected to Cole or </span>
  <span id="freeText6058076722813632250" style="display:none">I still cannot believe I am giving a Woodiwiss book only 2 stars. It seemed to me that part one and part two were written at completely different times. Alaina jumps back and forth between really caring for Cole, to not at all. There seemed to be so many plot lines throughout the book, that the characters suffered for it. The unlikely events that happened to coincide with one another were unbelievable at best, and the villains in the story were not thought out. I never felt connected to Cole or Alania , at all. I hated the "I am drunk and will take you" thing that happens, and his sloppy maneuvering was embarrassing. I am not a fan of sloppy drunks, and I felt his character was weak, as well as the countless things that happened to both of them. Of course there were misconceptions and they misunderstood each other at every turn, like a soap opera. The second part of the book has Alaina rude, angry and holding herself back from physical pleasure because of a misunderstanding. How she trusted what her uncle said was beyond believable, and quite surprising that she was suppose to be smart, but could not just come out and ask Cole about the marriage. Too many things happening in the story to make it real for me, and the way that black people were represented and the fact she used the words White Trash threw me. I don't think that black men would act like neanderthals and it made me uncomfortable. I do not think they would speak like a schooled white person in those times, but I doubt they would basically say and act like they were unable to form sentences. Me Tarzan, You Jane, kind of writing was not giving the characters credit. I am tolerant to a lot of things, but that was too much. <br /><br />All in all, I read it. I enjoyed the south vs north, but throwing facts in the story, does not make the story rich for me at all. Unfortunately it was just not a good read for me. </span>
  <a data-text-id="6058076722813632250" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer11170005817986381629">This was never my favorite KW book, but upon rereading it, I realized that I hadn’t remembered all of the problems! Definitely issues with consent, rape culture, “she said no but she meant yes,” blackface, revisionist civil war history, and plenty of near-plagiarism scenes/dialogue from GWTW. Whew, it was a lot. And usually, because it’s fiction, I can set those concerns aside and just enjoy the book (for what it is and when and why it was written) but the story here wasn’t great either: It was </span>
  <span id="freeText11170005817986381629" style="display:none">This was never my favorite KW book, but upon rereading it, I realized that I hadn’t remembered all of the problems! Definitely issues with consent, rape culture, “she said no but she meant yes,” blackface, revisionist civil war history, and plenty of near-plagiarism scenes/dialogue from GWTW. Whew, it was a lot. And usually, because it’s fiction, I can set those concerns aside and just enjoy the book (for what it is and when and why it was written) but the story here wasn’t great either: It was all over the place - and I caught myself skimming pages by the end. Did not love either main character, and found the banter between the two rather cringeworthy. Apparently these must’ve been just a few of the reasons why I had no fond memories of this book! Can’t win them all, I guess, on to the next! <br /><br />Three (disappointed, but still rounded up) stars.</span>

<div id="review_3483212386" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3483212386" />
    <a title="Jordan" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1664992-jordan"><img alt="Jordan" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1559239322p2/1664992.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3483212386?book_show_action=true">Aug 06, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jordan" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jordan" href="/user/show/1664992-jordan">Jordan</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3483212386" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14567731245880015312">The first half of this long book, (which could have been a book all on its own) was probably 4 stars for me. It was interesting, and a bit different, there was some adventure surrounding the war that added something. The characters made some obvious mistakes and there were some very unlikely happenings, but overall I liked the main characters and was interested to see how things would play out for them. The second half was largely an exercise in poor decisions and frustration, and got even less </span>
  <span id="freeText14567731245880015312" style="display:none">The first half of this long book, (which could have been a book all on its own) was probably 4 stars for me. It was interesting, and a bit different, there was some adventure surrounding the war that added something. The characters made some obvious mistakes and there were some very unlikely happenings, but overall I liked the main characters and was interested to see how things would play out for them. The second half was largely an exercise in poor decisions and frustration, and got even less believable. They kind of stopped seeming like part of a greater struggle (with the war and all) and focused almost entirely just on the ongoing drama of their own relationship. Which could have been almost entirely avoided any number of times by a single adult conversation. =/ All the characters are pretty solidly all good or all bad, which isn't quite as interesting to me, but it wasn't too bad. It ended up feeling quite Nancy Drew overall (especially the second half), with a long series of unlikely events each signaling future reveals, with a huge mystery/villain confrontation scene in the end. It wasn't really my thing, but I don't think I'll forget these two characters right away. I'm happy I read it, but I'm not likely to ever read it again. I would consider another from this author though.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14567731245880015312" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2936433590" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer678565343085686408">This is a tough one to review for me. I don’t typically read the romance genre and I also don’t read a lot of stories set in the Civil War but my book club chose it for this month and I’m always willing to try something different. I liked the author’s writing style as it felt very smooth. I wish the book had been quite a bit shorter - there were several slow parts (including much of the first part of the book). Most of the main characters were very well developed but I had a hard time rooting fo</span>
  <span id="freeText678565343085686408" style="display:none">This is a tough one to review for me. I don’t typically read the romance genre and I also don’t read a lot of stories set in the Civil War but my book club chose it for this month and I’m always willing to try something different. I liked the author’s writing style as it felt very smooth. I wish the book had been quite a bit shorter - there were several slow parts (including much of the first part of the book). Most of the main characters were very well developed but I had a hard time rooting for many of them - many maddening choices and interactions. The second part of the book was better and the ending was good but seemed a little rushed. All in all it was an interesting storyline and if you like drawn out stories with good character development you’ll probably like this. </span>
  <a data-text-id="678565343085686408" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

The female main character was a strong minded southerner and of course the main male character a yankee war doctor. I was loving this story and then 3/4 of the way through it felt like someone else started writing this book and it took a nosedive. Overall not a bad read. </span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('Qv3WwhtskBAk9iV+JxOnxSKgBr6EP4IXenm2oMceXCPHEq3OfMrIrbBfZAdnMyzoyOr1bQjxA2qdownmJd3eQw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('hFXx1Q98JSlwTXc4tXGVt3QomPUc4MguqJSXicf/GjIBuorZaNp9lOTkNkH1UR6anmJrJpAuSVNPTijPJTyYUg==')})

Such uncontrolled desires can lead only to dangerous misunderstandings and, perhaps, to a love that can live only once in a lifetime.<\/span>\n  <a data-text-id=\"14824169932018244494\" href=\"#\"       <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/88445.Kathleen_E_Woodiwiss">About Kathleen E. Woodiwiss</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/88445.Kathleen_E_Woodiwiss"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1237691529p3/88445.jpg);'></div>
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__widgetContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__name'>
<a href="/author/show/88445.Kathleen_E_Woodiwiss">Kathleen E. Woodiwiss
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__followerCount'>
1,450
followers
</div>

</div>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer14047763787146771679">Kathleen Erin Hogg was born on June 3, 1939, in Alexandria, Louisiana, she was the youngest of eight siblings by Gladys (Coker) and Charles Wingrove Hogg, a disabled World War I veteran. She long relished creating original narratives, and by age 6 was telling herself stories at night to help herself fall asleep. At age 16, she met U.S. Air Force Second Lieutenant Ross Eugene Woodiwiss at a dance, </span>
  <span id="freeText14047763787146771679" style="display:none">Kathleen Erin Hogg was born on June 3, 1939, in Alexandria, Louisiana, she was the youngest of eight siblings by Gladys (Coker) and Charles Wingrove Hogg, a disabled World War I veteran. She long relished creating original narratives, and by age 6 was telling herself stories at night to help herself fall asleep. At age 16, she met U.S. Air Force Second Lieutenant Ross Eugene Woodiwiss at a dance, and they married the following year. She wrote her first book in longhand while living at a military outpost in Japan.<br /><br />She is credited with the invention of the modern historical romance novel: In 1972 she released The Flame and the Flower, an instant New York Times bestseller that created a literary precedent. The novel revolutionized mainstream publishing, featuring an epic historical romance with a strong heroine and impassioned sex scenes. The Flame and the Flower was rejected by agents and hardcover publishers, who deemed it as "too long" at 600 pages. Rather than follow the advice of the rejection letters and rewrite the novel, she instead submitted it to paperback publishers. The first publisher on her list, Avon, quickly purchased the novel and arranged an initial 500,000 print run. The novel sold over 2.3 million copies in its first four years of publication.<br /><br />The success of The Flame and the Flower prompted a new style of writing romance, concentrating primarily on historical fiction tracking the monogamous relationship between a helpless heroines and the hero who rescued her, even if he had been the one to place her in danger. The romance novels which followed in her example featured longer plots, more controversial situations and characters, and more intimate and steamy sex scenes.<br /><br />She was an avid horse rider who at one time lived in a large home on 55 acres (220,000 m2) in Minnesota. After her husband's death in 1996, she moved back to Louisiana. She died in a hospital on July 6, 2007 in Princeton, Minnesota, aged 68, from cancer. She was survived by two sons, Sean and Heath, their wives, and numerous grandchildren. Her third son, Dorren, predeceased her.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="14047763787146771679" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>
</div>
